## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task models the rate of change of a chemical species concentration as a function of time and current concentration. The rate law dA/dt = f(A, t) encompasses standard kinetic orders, autocatalytic reactions, and potentially time-dependent rate processes.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A (rate proportional to concentration)
- Second-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (rate proportional to concentration squared)
- nth-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (generalized power-law rate)
- Mixed-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) (saturation kinetics for single species)
- Autocatalytic with decay: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (logistic-type, product-dependent feedback)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (forward and reverse first-order reaction)
- Consecutive reaction contribution: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (intermediate species dynamics)
- Time-dependent rate: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (rate constant changing with time)
- Cubic autocatalysis: dA_dt = c0 * A**3 + c1 * A**2 + c2 * A (third-order with multiple pathways)
- Square-root kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**0.5 (half-order, surface-mediated reactions)
- Competitive inhibition form: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 / (c1 + A) (second-order with saturation)
- Damped oscillatory rate: dA_dt = c0 * A * sin(c1 * t + c2) (periodic forcing or oscillating reactions)
- Polynomial rate law: dA_dt = c0 + c1 * A + c2 * A**2 (quadratic approximation of complex mechanism)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope â†’ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects â†’ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay â†’ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior â†’ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects â†’ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Simple integer-order kinetics â†’ Power law dA_dt = c * A**n where n is 0, 1, 2, or 3 corresponding to elementary reaction molecularity
- Equilibrium approach / reversible reactions â†’ Linear combination of forward and reverse terms: c0*A + c1 or c0*A - c1*A**2
- Autocatalytic or self-limiting behavior â†’ Product of concentration with a depletion term: A*(c0 - c1*A)
- Intermediate species in consecutive reactions â†’ Time-explicit exponential terms combined with concentration: f(A) + g(exp(c*t))
- Fractional reaction orders â†’ Non-integer powers A**c1 arising from complex multi-step mechanisms or surface reactions
- Conservation constraints (closed system) â†’ Rate expressions where A and (c - A) appear together, reflecting total mass conservation
- Oscillatory chemical dynamics (e.g., Belousov-Zhabotinsky) â†’ Trigonometric or nonlinear feedback terms involving both t and A
- Diffusion-limited kinetics â†’ Square root or fractional power dependence on concentration: A**0.5
